RatioOfTheDecision	These decisions deal with the jurisdiction of the appointed <ORG>, viz., whether the <ORG> has exceeded its jurisdiction or has failed to exercise its jurisdiction.
RatioOfTheDecision	In the present case,, the question for consideration is the provision of the Constitution which under some Articles confer jurisdiction on this <ORG> and in another Article excludes' the jurisdiction of the <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	A privative clause of this nature in the Constitution stands on an entirely different footing from a clause of that nature in other statutes.
RatioOfTheDecision	In ordinary statues, statutory authorities are entrusted with powers and duties.
RatioOfTheDecision	When a f inality clause appears in such statutes, the courts interfere with acts or decisions of such statutory bodies or authorities,- by issuing writs of mandamus, prohibition or certiorari, on the grounds of commanding them to exercise their jurisdiction or not to exceed their jurisdiction or not to usurp any jurisdiction they do not possess or to observe the principles of natural justice or where the courts find that the acts of decisions are tainted by extraneous consideration or collateral reasons or malafide or fraud.
RatioOfTheDecision	In the present case, the petitioners have invoked the juris- diction of this Court under Article 32.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 32 , is excluded by the opening words in Article 363.
RatioOfTheDecision	It was said by counsel for the petitioner that the order of the President was a nullity, the petitioners property rights were invaded, and,' therefore, the jurisdiction of this Court was attracted.
RatioOfTheDecision	The fallacy of the petitioner"s submission is in totally overlooking the provisions of Article 363 which exclude in express and unambiguous  terms the jurisdiction of this <ORG> notwithstanding any provision of the Constitution.
RatioOfTheDecision	The courts normally leap in favour of stretching the jurisdiction but when the Constitution which invests this <ORG> with jurisdiction with one hand divests it of jurisdiction with another in specifically designated disputes the attempt to overreach the Article which bars jurisdiction of courts will be totally impermissible.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is at this stage that the words of <NAME> in <ORG> v. Douds(1) will throw light.
RatioOfTheDecision	"The provisions of the Constitution are not mathematical formulae having their essence in their form; they are organic living institutions transplanted from English soil.
RatioOfTheDecision	Their significance is Vital, not formal; it is to be gathered not simply by (1) 339 U.S. 382 L744Sup.CI/71 taking the words and a dictionary, but by considering their origin and the line of growth".
RatioOfTheDecision	Therefore, if the Constitution has placed a restriction on the jurisdiction of this <ORG>, it will he trifling and tinkering with the  Constitution if this <ORG> interfered, in matters which were excluded from jurisdiction.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is well-settled that what is forbidden directly cannot be achieved indirectly.
RatioOfTheDecision	In interpretting these four allied Articles when this <ORG> finds that it has no jurisdiction it will say so and in saying so, the jurisdiction of this <ORG> is not whistled down in any manner.'
RatioOfTheDecision	The jurisdiction of this <ORG> is all pervasive and all embracing in regard to fundamental rights of citizens.
Argument	The petitioners are citizens but the rights they claim are recognition of rulership, payment of privy purse and enjoyment of princely privileges which are not fundamental rights on account of unenforceability.
Argument	These special rights belong to a world of their own and that is, why the makers of the Constitution intertwined Article 363 with the allied Articles 291, 363, 366(22) as the forbidden frontiers of <ORG>s.
Argument	It is now to be found out whether there are disputes with regard to payment of privy purses and whether such disputes can be said  to arise out of the provisions of this Constitution, and thirdly Whether the provisions of the Constitution in Article 291 relate to covenants and merger agreements.. Mr. <NAME> contended that there were no disputes as to payment of privy purses.
RatioOfTheDecision	This submission is unacceptable.
RatioOfTheDecision	The petitioner's claim in the petition to continue to be recognised a Ruler is for the purpose of payment of privy purse.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is not suggested that a recognition, of Ruler is in the abstract.
RatioOfTheDecision	A recognition of a Ruler is not by itself property.
RatioOfTheDecision	When there has been an order of recognition of a Ruler the Ruler then becomes, en- titled to payment of privy purse and enjoyment of other rights and privileges mentioned in Articles 291 and 362 respectively.
RatioOfTheDecision	For days there were discussions, debates and disputes at the <ORG> as to whether there were disputes as to privy purses.
RatioOfTheDecision	The pleading and the affidavit evidence point with unerring accuracy that the petitioners claim privy purse, assert title to privy purse and insist on payment of privy p urse guaranteed in covenants and merger agreements and recognised in Article 291 and by reason of provisions contained in Article 366(22) which speaks of recognition of Rulers they ask for relief with regard to continuance of recognition of Rulers and payment of privy purses.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is indisputable that the merger agreements and covenants not only speak of payment of privy purse but also mention guarantee of the <ORG> in that behalf.
RatioOfTheDecision	These covenants and merger agreements were totally unenforceable prior to the Constitution.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 291 is a constitutional recognition of the guarantee regarding privy purse mentioned in the Covenants and agreements.
Statute	Article 291 does not create any new 'and independent right of payment of privy purse.
Statute	Article 291 is related to the covenant and is not unrelated to the covenants and merger agreements.
Statute	When Article 291 was introduced in <ORG> as Article 267 it was said to give constitutional recognition to those guarantees and to provide for the expenses being  charged on the central revenues subject to such recoveries as might be made from time to time from the <ORG>s in respect of these payments.
Statute	Article, 291(2) as it stood at the time of the commencement of the Constitution indicated that where territories of any Indian <ORG> are comprised within a <ORG> specified in Part A or Part B of the First Schedule, there shall be charged.
Statute	on and paid out of the consolidated fund of that <ORG> such contribution, if any, in respect of the payments made by <ORG> under clause (1) and for such period as, may, subject to any agreement entered into that behalf under clause (1) of Article 278 be determined by order of the President.
Statute	Article 278 of the Constitution as it stood in 1950 provided that <ORG> might, subject to the pro- visions of clause (2) of Article 278 enter into an agreement with <ORG> specified in Part B of the First Schedule with respect to inter alia the contribution by such <ORG> in respect of any paymen t made by <ORG> under clause (1) of Article 291 and when an agreement was so, entered into the provisions of Chapter I of Part XII of the Constitution (Articles 264 to 291 under the title Finance) shall in relation to such States have effect subject to the terms of such agreement.
Precedent	Article 278 and Article 291 (2) were omitted, by the Constitution (Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956 in the year 1956.
Precedent	By the same Constitution (Seventh Amendment Act, 1956 the First Schedule to the Constitution 'as it originally stood consisting of Parts A, B and C in regard to the States and the, territories of India was repealed and substituted by the First' Schedule containing the States and the Union territories.
Precedent	These provisions in the Constitution as they stood in 1950 indicated that Article 291 embodied the constitutional recognition for the fulfilment of the guarantees and assurances given by <ORG> in respect of privy purses and provided for necessary adjustments in respect of privy purse enta iled by changed circumstance and conditions.
RatioOfTheDecision	222  This Court has held in <CITATION_1953650> .
RatioOfTheDecision	(1) that in order to give constitutional recognition to the guarantees and assurances under the Covenants and Merger Agreement Articles 362, 363, 131 proviso and 291 were incor- porated in the Constitution.
RatioOfTheDecision	The Covenants and Merger Agreements did not have any legal sanction inasmuch as neither the Government of India Act, 1935 provided for the same nor were these enforceable in municipal courts.
RatioOfTheDecision	The sanction of the Covenants and Merger Agreements was purely political.
RatioOfTheDecision	The treaties in the United States are enforced as law.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is not so in our Constitution nor is it so under the British law.
RatioOfTheDecision	During the British Rule in India political pensions were given to persons in Indian States.
RatioOfTheDecision	They were given because of reasons of State policy.
RatioOfTheDecision	When the Constitution came into force the guarantee for the payment of the sums of money as privy purse contained in the Covenants and Agreements was continued by Article 291 but the esenti al political character of the privy purse was pre- served by Article 363 by enacting that the guarantee could not be enforced in municipal courts.
RatioOfTheDecision	It might be asked here as to whether any Ruler of an Indian 'State without being recognised a Ruler by the President could I prefer any claim to privy purse under Article 291.
RatioOfTheDecision	The answer would be.
RatioOfTheDecision	in the negative, because the words of Article 291 in the Constitution predicate that where under any agreement or covenant entered into by the Ruler of an Indian State before the commencement of the Constitution the payment of any sum free of tax has been guaranteed or assured to any Ruler of such State, as privy purse (a) such sums shall be charged on and paid out of the consolidated fund of India and (b) the sums so paid to any Ruler shall be exempt from all taxes on income.
RatioOfTheDecision	The Ruler of an.
RatioOfTheDecision	Indian State mentioned in the first part of Article 291 is different to the Ruler mentioned in Article 291 (b).
RatioOfTheDecision	The latter refers to the Ruler defined under Article 366(22) and rec ognised by the President.
RatioOfTheDecision	At once the provisions of Article 366(22) are attracted to find out as to who that Ruler is.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is a Ruler who is recognised by the President 'as the Ruler of the State.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is because of the combined effect of Articles 291.
Precedent	366(22) and 363 that this Court in <CITATION_793151> (supra) held that privy purse was paid for political ,consideration and was not a right legally enforceable in any, municipal court and the political character was preserved by Article-363 by taking privy purse beyond the reach of courts of law.
Precedent	In Sri sudhansu <CITATION_1414177> .
Precedent	(2) this Court said on a consideration of Articles 291 (1)  5 S.C.R.
Precedent	1 (2)  1 S.C.R.
Precedent	779 and 362 that if in disregard of the guarantee or assurance given under the, covenant or agreement any legislation were made it could not be questioned in Court because of Article  363.
Argument	It is true that Article 362 speaks of guarantee of rights other than that of privy purse.
Argument	It was said on behalf of the petitioner that the words "charged on and pa id out of the consolidated fund" in Article 291 meant that a security was created in favour of the petitioner in respect of privy purse, and, therefore, a new and independent right was created.
Argument	It was said that Article 291 was a self sustaining or self ordaining provision.
Argument	Article 291 draws its sustenance and vitality from covenants and merger agreements.
Argument	If payment has not been guaranteed under the covenants or merger agreements, Article 291 does not come into operation at all.
Argument	Under Article 291 effect is to be given to the covenants and merger agreements where payment of any sum has been guranteed.
RatioOfTheDecision	Each covenant has to be examined and construed to give effect to the guarantee mentioned in the covenant 'and recognised in the Article.
RatioOfTheDecision	It will be utterly wrong to equate the words "charged on the consolidated fund" with "a charge by way of security", because Article 291 only gives effect to guarantees in the covenants and agreements by charging the payment on the consolidated Fund.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 291 cannot be said to  create a new right or a new obligation by charging the sum on the consolidated fund because the charge is only in respect of the right and obligation under the covenant and it is therefore neither a new nor an independent right.
RatioOfTheDecision	It was said that the covenants and merger agreements were merely to be referred to for the purpose of identifying the Rulers and the privy purse.
RatioOfTheDecision	The identification is a verbal subterfuge.
RatioOfTheDecision	Assuming Article 291 were a right enforceable a Ruler would have to prove first that he was a Ruler who was recognised by the President and thus entitled to privy purse the payment of whereof was guaranteed by the covenant or the merger agreement.
RatioOfTheDecision	Secondly, he would have to prove the covenant whereby he claimed 'a privy purse.
RatioOfTheDecision	For that again be would have to prove on the strength of the covenant or the merger agreement.
RatioOfTheDecision	Proof is in aid of title.
RatioOfTheDecision	Proof is not dissociated from claim.
RatioOfTheDecision	Claim will fail without proof.
RatioOfTheDecision	Therefore, covenants and merger agreements are indissolubly bound up with Article 291.
RatioOfTheDecision	Again, there were different merger I agreements with different <ORG> providing for different sums for payment to the <ORG> and also in some cases for payment of different sums to successors.
RatioOfTheDecision	The Orissa and Chattisgarh Merger Agreement did not mention about payment of privy purse to the successors to <ORG>.
Fact	The Tehri Garhwal Merger Agreement mentioned also the heirs 'and successors of the <NAME> for payment of privy purse.
Fact	The Rampur Merger Agreement mentioned certain amount as privy purse for the <NAME> and a different sum for payment to the successors.
Fact	The Bhopal Merger Agreement mentioned a certain sum for the <NAME> and a different sum for the <NAME> and a different sum for his successor.
Fact	The Agreement of Himachal Pradesh <ORG> mentioned a certain sum for the Ruler but did not mention 'about successors.
Precedent	The Bilaspur Merger Agreement mentioned a certain sum as privy purse of.
Precedent	the <ORG> which was to include the allowances of the Yuvraja but did not mention anything about successors.
RatioOfTheDecision	These difference illu strate that Article 291 is vitally related to the covenants and merger agreements and draw substance from them.
RatioOfTheDecision	The words "charged on and paid out of the consolidated fond" in Article 291 mean that the sum shall not be submitted to the vote of <ORG>, and Article 113(1) makes a provision to that effect.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 291 does not by itself create any independent right of any Ruler to be paid any sum out of any charged fund.
RatioOfTheDecision	If it were a charge, it would be a debt which would be assignable.
RatioOfTheDecision	It a Ruler were to 'assign or mortgage or create a charge in respect of his privy purse in favour of another person there would have been no legal validity for such assignment and mortgage or charge.
RatioOfTheDecision	The reason is that there is no vested legal right in praosenti in favour of a Ruler.
RatioOfTheDecision	Again, a privy purse is a payment of a political character and is legally unenforceable.
RatioOfTheDecision	There is no right either in rem or in personam in favour of a Ruler in regard to payment of privy purse.
RatioOfTheDecision	Supposing the privy purse were reduced would it be  competent to a Ruler to maintain an action for payment of the entire sum.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 363 would be an impediment and no court would be able to adjudicate the question.
RatioOfTheDecision	The words "charged on and paid out of the consolidated fund" are technical Parliamentary ex- pressions for payment out of public revenues.
RatioOfTheDecision	These words have been borrowed from <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	These words have a specific legal history since 1816 when Consolidated Fund Act was passed in England and in 1854 the English Act provided in 2 Schedules as charges, payable out of the consolidated Fund and charges upon which vote would lie.
RatioOfTheDecision	Prior to 1935 the system of presenting accounts before the legislature was under four heads, i.e.
RatioOfTheDecision	transferred subjects, reserved subjects voted 'and non-voted items.
RatioOfTheDecision	In 1935 the Government Act , 1935 used the expressed "charged" in replacement of ,the expression "voted".
RatioOfTheDecision	After the Constitution came into existence the same system continued for presentation of the Annual Financial Statement under Article 112( 2) and Appropriation Bill under Article 114(1).
RulingByLowerCourt	The Estimates under Article 113(1)  were (a) sums required to meet the expenses as expenditure charged upon the consolidated fund and (b) the sum required to meet the other expenditure proposed to be met from the consolidated fund.
RulingByLowerCourt	The Appropriation Bill means (a) the grants made by <ORG>; and (b) the expenditure charged on the consolidated fund but not exceeding in any case the amount shown in the statement previously laid before <ORG>.
RulingByLowerCourt	Article 113 says that so much of the estimates as relates to expenditure charged upon the, consolidated fund shall not be submitted to the vote of <ORG> but there is nothing to prevent discussion in either House of <ORG> of any of those estimates.
RulingByLowerCourt	The expenditure is charged and removed from the vote of <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	In the English <ORG>ary Practice what is charged is the expenditure that is to be made without vote of <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	These are first, a sum appropriated to a particular service whic h cannot be spent on another service, secondly, the sum appropriated is the maximum sum, and thirdly, it is available only in respect of charges which have arisen during one of the years to which the relevant Appropriation Act applies (See May Parliamentary Practice, 17th ed.
RatioOfTheDecision	713).
RatioOfTheDecision	The tests used to determine whether the expenditure involves a charge on the consolidated fund are that a charge must be new and distinct, that it must be payable out of the exchequer and it is to be effectively imposed.
Statute	In England it will appear that the Ministers of the Crown Act, 1937 in section 4 enacts that a pension under that section is payable as of :right.
Statute	Section 7 of that English Act of 1937 used the expression "shall be charged and payable out of the consolidated fund".
RatioOfTheDecision	These provisions in the English Act show first that the right to be paid is under section 4 and the creation of a charge on the consolidated fund is under section 7 .
RatioOfTheDecision	The words "charged on the Consolidated fund" in Article 291 mean that the expenditure  is non-votable and these are terms of public finance.
RatioOfTheDecision	Charge on <ORG> is an accounting arrangement before <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	Certain expen- diture is authorised out of public revenue as independent of <ORG>ary control.
RatioOfTheDecision	Charge is meant for expenditure.
RatioOfTheDecision	The words "paid out of the consolidated fund" denote the source from which the expenditure will be met.
RatioOfTheDecision	The words "charged and paid out of the consolidated funs' do not create any legal right in a party.
RatioOfTheDecision	The right to payment arises dehors the charge on the consolidated fund.
RatioOfTheDecision	The charge on the consolidated Fund is for purposes of payment in 'accordance with the guarantee and assurance of payment under the covenants and merger agreements.
RatioOfTheDecision	The right to payment of privy purse arises from recognition by Article 291 of guarantee of payment of privy purse under a covenant.
RatioOfTheDecision	The scheme of Article 291 is similar to Article 290 where the expenses of any court or commission or pension payable to any person who served before or after the commencement of the Con stitution in connection with the affairs of the <ORG> or the <ORG> are charged on the <ORG> fund.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 290A which speaks of a sum of Rs.
RatioOfTheDecision	46,50,000 to be charged on and paid out of the <ORG> Fund of the <ORG> of Kerala every year to <ORG> is a different provision because it speaks of payment to a designated person as a part of the Constitution.
RatioOfTheDecision	No such comparable words are to be found in Article 291 , namely, that the sums shall be paid to the Rulers.
RatioOfTheDecision	The reasons are two-fold.
RatioOfTheDecision	First, payment of privy purses is under covenants or merger agreements and secondly these payments were charged on the <ORG> Fund of India because the payment was not out of the <ORG> Fund of any <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	Originally, Article 291 contained the expression "paid out of" in both sub-clause (a) of clause (1) and clause (2) of Article 291 for the purpose of integration of finances, assets, and liabilities of the new Constitution as between <ORG> at the <ORG> and <ORG> tes which guaranteed payment of Privy Purse under covenants and merger agreements.
RatioOfTheDecision	The original Article 291 was the result of the decision of <ORG> regarding sharing between <ORG> and <ORG> and Part B States regarding privy purse.
Argument	Counsel on behalf of the petitioner submitted that unless the words "charged on and paid out of the consolidated fund" mean security and right to be paid neither the President, nor the Chairman or Deputy Chairman, nor the Speaker and the Deputy Speaker, nor the Judges of <ORG>, nor the Comptroller and Auditor General would have security as to payments.
RatioOfTheDecision	But, these persons do not derive their right to be paid from any covenant or merger agreement.
RatioOfTheDecision	Secondly, these persons hold offices under the Constitution whereas the Rulers do not.
RatioOfTheDecision	Thirdly, Articles 59(3), 97, 125, 148(3) indicate in no uncertain terms that they shall be entitled to such emoluments and allowances and privileges as may be determined by P arliament by law.
RatioOfTheDecision	In the case of the President, the Chairman, the Deputy Chairman of <ORG>, the Speaker and the Deputy Speaker of <ORG> Articles 59 (3) and 97 provide that there, shall be paid to them such allowances and salaries as may be fixed by <ORG>, by law and until the provision in that behalf is so made such salaries and allowances as are specified in the Second Schedule.
Statute	As for the Judges of this Court Article 125(1) enacts that there shall be paid to the Judges of this Court, such salaries as are specified in the Second Schedule.
Statute	Article 148(3) enacts that the salaries and other conditions of the Comptroller and Auditor General shall be such as may be determined by <ORG> and until they are so determined, shall be as specified in the Second Schedule.
RatioOfTheDecision	Therefore, it was an unfortunate comparison made by Mr. <NAME> between these persons and the <NAME>.
RatioOfTheDecision	To illustrate, some of these persons become entitled to salaries by virtue of provision in the Constituti on, e.g.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 1.25 directing payment of their salaries and therefore the charge on <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	in respect of such salaries e.g.
Statute	in Article 112 (d)   (i) cannot be intended again as a diction for payment.
Argument	It was said on behalf of the petitioner that in the covenants and merger agreements, the payment of privy purse was to be free of all taxes whereas under the Constitution privy purse was to be exempt free of all taxes on income and therefore there was a new right.
RatioOfTheDecision	This is totally misreading Article 291 (b) where it is said that "the sums so paid to any Ruler shall be exempt from all taxes on income".
RatioOfTheDecision	The words "so paid' relate to the slum guaranteed under the covenants and the agreements and to the same sum charged on <ORG> It is only when payment is made to a Ruler that it shall be exempt from taxes on income That is why the words "so paid to any Ruler" in Article 291 (b) indicate that when the sums are paid to a Ruler out of <ORG> the sums shall be exempt from a ll taxes.
RatioOfTheDecision	The Constitution does not mention payment of Privy Purse to any particular person.
RatioOfTheDecision	One has to turn to the covenant and the merger agreement to have all the particulars of persons, sums guaranteed and assured.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 291 does not create any new and independent right but it merely gives constitutional recognition to guarantees under covenants and merger agreements which Were and are unenforceable as those arise, out of Acts of State.
RatioOfTheDecision	( <CITATION_19878> (supra).
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 291 is strung with the covenants because such sums in Article 291 (a) mean the sums guaranteed under covenants and merger agreements.
RatioOfTheDecision	The fons et origo is the guarantee contained in the Covenants and Agreements.
Argument	Another argument was advanced on behalf of the petitioner that there was a substitution of rights under covenants and merger agreements by Article 291.
RatioOfTheDecision	The rights guaranteed under the covenants and merger agreements are matters to which Article 291 relates.
RatioOfTheDecision	The guarantee of payment under the covenants and merger agreements is  recognised under Article 291.
RatioOfTheDecision	This Article gives effect to the covenants and agreements and it is related to these.
RatioOfTheDecision	There were some arguments that if the amount charged on the consolidated fund on account of privy purse were not paid, the same would be carried over, in <ORG> from year to year.
RatioOfTheDecision	That is not so because any sum charged on the consolidated fund is not carried to the next year but it lapses.
Argument	Article 362 has been held by this <ORG> in Udaipur case (supra) to fall within Article 363.
Argument	Article 291 has also been held by this <ORG> to fall within the bar of Article 363 in <NAME> case (supra).
Argument	It was suggested that the only Article which could fall within Article 363 was Article 362 which was in closest proximity.
Argument	That would be an erroneous approach to interpret the Constitution.
Argument	Article 363 uses the words "provisions- of the Constitution".
Argument	The word "provisions" indicate more than one Article.
Argument	Even at the risk of repetition it has to be stated that Articles 291, 362 and  366(22) have a most direct and visible relation to Article 363.
Argument	Mr. <NAME> contended that the petitioner had existing rights to privy purge and privileges prior to the Constitution and that such existing rights were incorporated in the Constitution by Articles 294 (b) and 295 (1 ) (b) of the Constitution.
Argument	It.
RatioOfTheDecision	has been consistently held by this <ORG> that till recognition, either express or implied, is granted by the new sovereign, the Act of State continues ( <CITATION_19878> (supra).
RatioOfTheDecision	Therefore, the covenants and merger agreements were outside the jurisdiction of municipal courts.
RatioOfTheDecision	The administration of the provincially merged and centrally merged States was by reason of the Extra Provincial Jurisdiction Act 1947 which applied the laws of the Dominion of India to those merged States.
RatioOfTheDecision	It was only by reason of the-merger agreement that the Dominion of India exercised such extra provincial jurisdiction.
RatioOfTheDecision	The Instruments of Accession did not confer such authority.
RatioOfTheDecision	Even when sections 290A and 290B were introdu ced in the Government of India Act, 1935 administration in the provincially merged <ORG>s was still carried on the strength of the merger agreement.
RatioOfTheDecision	(See Seraikela case (supra).
RatioOfTheDecision	The merged <ORG>s were not yet completely integrated with India.
Statute	The <ORG>s Merger (Governors' Provinces) Order, 1949 stated that as from the appointed day, i.e.,the date of the com- mencement of the order 1 August, 1949, the <ORG>s specified in the Schedule "shall be administered in all respects as if they form part of the provinces specified in the heading of the Schedule".
Statute	Again in section 7 of the <ORG>s Merger (Governors' Provinces) Order, 1949 it is stated that all liabilities in respect of loans, guarantees and other financial obligations of <ORG> as arise out of covenants, of a merged <ORG>, including in particular the liability for the payment of any sums to the Ruler of the merged <ORG> on account of his privy purse or to persons in the merged <ORG> on account of political pensions and the like shall as fr om the appointed day be liabilities of the absorbing <ORG> unless the loan, guarantee or other financial obligation is relateable to central purpose.
Statute	The privy purse is mentioned separately to and independently of loans, guarantees and other financial obligations.
Statute	The character of the liability regarding privy purse is not changed by the States (Merger Governors' <ORG>) Order, 1949.
RatioOfTheDecision	The Act of State which commenced with the Instruments of Accession continued even after the merger agreements as has been held by this Court in <NAME> case (supra).
RatioOfTheDecision	The liabilities in Articles 294 (b) and 295 (1 ) (b) of the Constitution refer to other legal rights which were enforceable in a court of law.
RatioOfTheDecision	Privy purses under the covenants and merger agreements were no such legal rights enforceable in a court of law for the obvious reason that if prior to the Constitution the covenants and merger agreements were sought to be enforced in a municipal, court the Government would have demurred on the plea of Act of Sta te.
Statute	That plea in bar would be available to <ORG> as a defence to any claim under Articles 294 (b) and 295 (1) (b).
Statute	( <CITATION_420189> .)
Statute	(1) Furthermore, Article 295 (1 ) (b) cannot apply because neither privy purse nor privileges are matters enumerated in the Union List.
Statute	Articles 291 and 362 are special provisions dealing with privy purses and privileges.
Statute	Articles 294(b) and 295(1) (b) deal with revolution of liabilities of the Dominion and Part B States respectively.
RulingByLowerCourt	The Constitution has dealt with privy purse and privileges in separate Articles.
RulingByLowerCourt	Therefore, Articles 294(b) and 295 (1 ) (b) can have no application to privy purses and Privileges.
RulingByLowerCourt	( <CITATION_1101230> .)
RulingByLowerCourt	2 ) where this Court held that Article 372 was a general provision and Article 277 was a special provision and a special provision was to be given effect to the extent of its scope, leaving  -the general provision to control cases where the special provision does not apply.
Fact	The petitioner's contention on existing rights prio r to the Constitution as well as continuance thereof falls.
RatioOfTheDecision	Agreement to pay privy purses and to continue privileges of the Princes which were.
RatioOfTheDecision	guaranteed by <ORG> before the Constitution- were all political agreements born out of political bargains to achieve integration of Indian States with the Dominion of India.
RatioOfTheDecision	This political bargain was carried into the Constitution by the insertion of Article 291 for payment of privy purse, Article 362 for continuance of privileges and Article 366(22) for recognition of princes, and the political character was preser-  [1] [1964] 7 S.C.R.

Argument	Mr. <NAME> contended that the order affected the rights of the petitioner under the Wealth Tax Act , the Income-tax Act , the Gift Tax Act , the Hindu Succession Act ,  the Estates Duty Act , Customs Regulation, Code of Civil Procedure, Code of Criminal Procedure and Madhya Bharat Gangajali Trust Fund Act, 1954.
RatioOfTheDecision	The Wealth Tax Act , 1957 defines a Ruler as defined in clause (22) of Article 366 of the Constitution and enacts certain exemptions in respect of certain assets namely the official residence in the occupation of the Ruler.
RatioOfTheDecision	The right of the petitioner under the Wealth Tax Act is dependent on being recognised as a Ruler by the President under Article 366(22).
RatioOfTheDecision	If the order cannot be challenged for the reasons given above, the petitioner can have no right under the Wealth Tax Act , because the right under the Wealth Tax Act is derived only from his recognition as a Ruler under Article 366(22).
Statute	Under the Income Tax Act , 1922 (, section 4(3)(x) ) and the Income Tax Act , 1961 ( section 10(19) amount received by a Ruler as privy purse is not in- clued as income.
Statute	Under Income Tax Part B States Taxation concessions Order, 1950 the bonafide annual value of the palaces decl ared by <ORG> as official residence of the Ruler is exempted from taxation.
RatioOfTheDecision	Therefore, if the rights are derived from recognition of Rulership by the President under Article 366(22) and if the recognition cannot be impeached no right arises.
RatioOfTheDecision	Under the Gift Tax Act , tax is not leviable on gifts out of privy purse for maintenance of relatives or for performance of official ceremonies.
RatioOfTheDecision	If no privy purse is paid no question of any gift out of privy purse arises.
RatioOfTheDecision	Under the Hindu Succession Act the Act shall not apply to any estate which descends to a single heir by the terms of any covenant or agreement.
RatioOfTheDecision	Succession is a right which can be claimed by heirs of the petitioners.
RatioOfTheDecision	The petitioners cannot have any fundamental right of any such right under the Hindu Succession Act .
RatioOfTheDecision	Under the Estates Duty Act , exemption is given in respect of any building in the occupation of a Ruler declared by <ORG> as his official residence.
RatioOfTheDecision	If the petitioner disposes of his property he will not be af fected.
RatioOfTheDecision	The duty will have to be paid by someone who will inherit or succeed.
RatioOfTheDecision	As for the Customs Regulations exemption is available only to Rulers recognised by the President.
RatioOfTheDecision	When he ceased to be recognised no exemption applies.
RatioOfTheDecision	The trust properties arise only in the case of Madhya Bharat Gangaiali Fund Trust Act, 1954.
RatioOfTheDecision	The Ruler of Gwalior is one of the trustees and is the President.
RatioOfTheDecision	The Trust will not fail.
RatioOfTheDecision	The trustees wilt con- tinue and the Act may have to be amended in a suitable manner.
RatioOfTheDecision	231  The Civil Procedure Code grants exemption to Rulers from being sued.
RatioOfTheDecision	Exemption from being sued is not personal liberty within the meaning of Article 21.
RatioOfTheDecision	Exemption from being sued is pro-cedural advantage which will no longer be available.
RatioOfTheDecision	Again, s. 197 of the Code of Criminal Procedure is a procedural advantage.
RatioOfTheDecision	In all these cases the petitioner cannot complain in this Court because the position is derived from the recognition of Rulership and Art.
RatioOfTheDecision	363 is an insurmountable and impenetrable bar.
RatioOfTheDecision	Recognition of Rul ership is not a legal right.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is not a right to property.
RatioOfTheDecision	Privy purse is not a legal right to property.
RatioOfTheDecision	There is no fundamental right to privy purse.
RatioOfTheDecision	There is no fundamental right to Rulership.- A series of decisions of this Court have held that Article 363 is a bar to rights and privileges, recognition of Rulership from being agitated in courts.
RatioOfTheDecision	These decisions have spoken the words of the Constitution.
RulingByPresentCourt	The petitions, therefore, fail and are dismissed.
RulingByPresentCourt	Each party will pay and bear its own costs.
